                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Independent Study Project (Undergraduate)</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1920 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13443]</span></h3>


  	Undergraduate Independent Study supervised by a member of the Italian Studies Faculty. Students may pursue independent research in order to prepare for their honors thesis or honors multimedia project, or they may enroll in the course in order to work individually with a faculty member on a specific area of Italian Studies not covered in the current course offerings.  Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Caroline+Castiglione">Caroline Castiglione</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Independent Study Project (Undergraduate)</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1920 S02 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13444]</span></h3>


  	Undergraduate Independent Study supervised by a member of the Italian Studies Faculty. Students may pursue independent research in order to prepare for their honors thesis or honors multimedia project, or they may enroll in the course in order to work individually with a faculty member on a specific area of Italian Studies not covered in the current course offerings.  Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Ronald+L+Martinez">Ronald L Martinez</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Independent Study Project (Undergraduate)</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1920 S03 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13445]</span></h3>


  	Undergraduate Independent Study supervised by a member of the Italian Studies Faculty. Students may pursue independent research in order to prepare for their honors thesis or honors multimedia project, or they may enroll in the course in order to work individually with a faculty member on a specific area of Italian Studies not covered in the current course offerings.  Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Suzanne+Stewart-Steinberg">Suzanne Stewart-Steinberg</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Independent Study Project (Undergraduate)</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1920 S04 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13446]</span></h3>


  	Undergraduate Independent Study supervised by a member of the Italian Studies Faculty. Students may pursue independent research in order to prepare for their honors thesis or honors multimedia project, or they may enroll in the course in order to work individually with a faculty member on a specific area of Italian Studies not covered in the current course offerings.  Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Massimo+Riva">Massimo Riva</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Independent Study Project (Undergraduate)</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1920 S05 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13447]</span></h3>


  	Undergraduate Independent Study supervised by a member of the Italian Studies Faculty. Students may pursue independent research in order to prepare for their honors thesis or honors multimedia project, or they may enroll in the course in order to work individually with a faculty member on a specific area of Italian Studies not covered in the current course offerings.  Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Filomena+Fantarella">Filomena Fantarella</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Senior Conference</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1990 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13448]</span></h3>


  	Special work or preparation of an honors thesis under the direction of a member of the staff. Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Caroline+Castiglione">Caroline Castiglione</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Senior Conference</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1990 S02 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13449]</span></h3>


  	Special work or preparation of an honors thesis under the direction of a member of the staff. Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Ronald+L+Martinez">Ronald L Martinez</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Senior Conference</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1990 S03 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13450]</span></h3>


  	Special work or preparation of an honors thesis under the direction of a member of the staff. Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Suzanne+Stewart-Steinberg">Suzanne Stewart-Steinberg</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Senior Conference</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1990 S04 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13451]</span></h3>


  	Special work or preparation of an honors thesis under the direction of a member of the staff. Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Massimo+Riva">Massimo Riva</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Senior Conference</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1990 S05 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 13452]</span></h3>


  	Special work or preparation of an honors thesis under the direction of a member of the staff. Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Cristina+Abbona-Sneider">Cristina Abbona-Sneider</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>I: Independent Study/Research</dd>
		
		


		</dl>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Preliminary Examination Preparation</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 2970 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 14998]</span></h3>


  	For graduate students who have met the tuition requirement and are paying the registration fee to continue active enrollment while preparing for a preliminary examination.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


		

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>E: Grad Enrollment Fee/Dist Prep</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Thesis Preparation</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 2990 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 14999]</span></h3>


  	For graduate students who have met the tuition requirement and are paying the registration fee to continue active enrollment while preparing a thesis.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


		

	
				
		
		
					<dt>Meeting Type</dt>
			<dd>E: Grad Enrollment Fee/Dist Prep</dd>
		
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Elementary Italian</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 0100 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 15042]</span></h3>


  	Elective for students without previous training in Italian. No credit for first semester alone. Fundamentals of Italian grammar and development of skills in speaking, comprehension, and writing. Overview of contemporary Italian society. Four meetings per week, audio and video work, two Italian films.  Note:  This is a year course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>18</dd>
		
					<dt>Course Attributes</dt>
						<dd>First Half of Year Course</dd>
			
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Cristina+Abbona-Sneider">Cristina Abbona-Sneider</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
														<dd>
						<div class="room"><a href="http://www.brown.edu/Facilities/Facilities_Management/maps/index.php?query=J. Walter Wilson">J. Walter Wilson</a> 401</div>
						<div class="times">13:00 - 13:50 Mon, Wed - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017						</div>
						</dd>
											<dd>
						<div class="room"><a href="http://www.brown.edu/Facilities/Facilities_Management/maps/index.php?query=J. Walter Wilson">J. Walter Wilson</a> 501</div>
						<div class="times">13:00 - 14:20 Tue, Thu - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017						</div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Elementary Italian</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 0100 S02 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 15043]</span></h3>


  	Elective for students without previous training in Italian. No credit for first semester alone. Fundamentals of Italian grammar and development of skills in speaking, comprehension, and writing. Overview of contemporary Italian society. Four meetings per week, audio and video work, two Italian films.  Note:  This is a year course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>18</dd>
		
					<dt>Course Attributes</dt>
						<dd>First Half of Year Course</dd>
			
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Cristina+Abbona-Sneider">Cristina Abbona-Sneider</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
														<dd>
						<div class="room"><a href="http://www.brown.edu/Facilities/Facilities_Management/maps/index.php?query=J. Walter Wilson">J. Walter Wilson</a> 401</div>
						<div class="times">09:00 - 10:20 Tue, Thu - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017						</div>
						</dd>
											<dd>
						<div class="room"><a href="http://www.brown.edu/Facilities/Facilities_Management/maps/index.php?query=J. Walter Wilson">J. Walter Wilson</a> 501</div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Elementary Italian</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 0100 S03 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 15044]</span></h3>


  	Elective for students without previous training in Italian. No credit for first semester alone. Fundamentals of Italian grammar and development of skills in speaking, comprehension, and writing. Overview of contemporary Italian society. Four meetings per week, audio and video work, two Italian films.  Note:  This is a year course.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>18</dd>
		
					<dt>Course Attributes</dt>
						<dd>First Half of Year Course</dd>
			
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Cristina+Abbona-Sneider">Cristina Abbona-Sneider</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
														<dd>
						<div class="room"><a href="http://www.brown.edu/Facilities/Facilities_Management/maps/index.php?query=J. Walter Wilson">J. Walter Wilson</a> 401</div>
						<div class="times">10:30 - 11:50 Tue, Thu - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017						</div>
						</dd>
											<dd>
						<div class="room"><a href="http://www.brown.edu/Facilities/Facilities_Management/maps/index.php?query=J. Walter Wilson">J. Walter Wilson</a> 501</div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Intermediate Italian I</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 0300 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 15045]</span></h3>


  	Review of the fundamentals of grammar, with emphasis on speaking and writing.  Reading of representative short stories.  Weekly compositions, presentations, and a paper.  Three Italian films.  Prerequisite:  ITAL 0100-0200, or ITAL 0110, or placement by examination.  Requirement for enrollment in the Bologna Program.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>18</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Cristina+Abbona-Sneider">Cristina Abbona-Sneider</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
									<dd>
						<span class="room"> </span>
						<span class="times">12:00 - 12:50 Mon, Tue, Wed, Thu - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017</span>
						</dd>
							
		
		
		
					<dt>Exam Group Code</dt>
			<dd>15</dd>
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Intermediate Italian I</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 0300 S02 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 15049]</span></h3>


  	Review of the fundamentals of grammar, with emphasis on speaking and writing.  Reading of representative short stories.  Weekly compositions, presentations, and a paper.  Three Italian films.  Prerequisite:  ITAL 0100-0200, or ITAL 0110, or placement by examination.  Requirement for enrollment in the Bologna Program.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>18</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Cristina+Abbona-Sneider">Cristina Abbona-Sneider</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
									<dd>
						<span class="room"> </span>
						<span class="times">11:00 - 11:50 Mon, Tue, Wed, Thu - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017</span>
						</dd>
							
		
		
		
					<dt>Exam Group Code</dt>
			<dd>15</dd>
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Advanced Italian I</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 0500 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 15051]</span></h3>


  	The purpose of this advanced course is to improve speaking and writing skills by offering extensive practice in a variety of styles and forms. Students will discuss various aspects of contemporary Italian culture. Reading, analysis and class discussion of texts (articles, songs, pictures, short stories, movies and television), oral presentations, based on research, and a writing portfolio (compositions, essays, blog and a journal). Prerequisites: ITAL 0400, or placement by examination.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>999</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>

			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
									<dd>
						<span class="room"> </span>
						<span class="times">12:00 - 12:50 Mon, Tue, Wed, Thu - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017</span>
						</dd>
							
		
		
		
					<dt>Exam Group Code</dt>
			<dd>12</dd>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Italian Identity</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1000G S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 16338]</span></h3>


  	This course examines the process of the construction of Italian identity from National Unification until today. Through a close reading of Manzoni, De Amicis, Verga and Lampedusa’s works, we investigate the formation of Italian identity through language, literature, food, and opera. We will also examine the problems of Post-Unification Italy: the economic and cultural gap between North and South and the Southern Issue. Finally, we will examine documentaries and readings that assess Italy today to analyze the feeling of not-belonging and estrangement, and the problematic search for a cohesive identity in a multicultural Italy within the European Union. Taught in Italian.

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Dante in English Translation: Dante's World and the Invention of Modernity</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1010 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 16339]</span></h3>


  	Primarily for students with no knowledge of Italian. Given in English. Concentrators in Italian should enroll in ITAL 1610; they are expected to read the material in the original. Close study and discussion of Dante's deployment of systems of retribution in the Inferno and rehabilitation in the Purgatorio with a view to imagining a society based on love and resistant to the effects of nascent capitalism and the money economy. Dante's work summarizes and transforms the entire ancient and medieval tradition of literature, philosophy, and science. WRIT
		
		

		<dl>

			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">The Divina Commedia: Inferno and Purgatorio</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 1610 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 16340]</span></h3>


  	A close reading of the first two canticles of Dante's poem in the light of contemporary European and American critical interpretations. In Italian. Enrollment limited to 40.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>40</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Ronald+L+Martinez">Ronald L Martinez</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
									<dd>
						<span class="room"> </span>
						<span class="times">16:00 - 18:30 Thu - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017</span>
						</dd>
							
		
		
		
					<dt>Exam Group Code</dt>
			<dd>04</dd>
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Introduction to Italian Studies</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 2100 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 16341]</span></h3>


  	This seminar, a requirement for graduate students in Italian Studies, has three objectives: 1) to provide a panoramic view of the current research in the interdisciplinary field of Italian studies (literature, history, arts and media); 2) to provide a picture of the professional state of the field, within the framework of more global developments in academia and the job markets; 3) to provide useful information about the resources and the new tools and techniques for research available to students at Brown and elsewhere (special collections in the Brown libraries, digital resources such as data bases, electronic journals, web projects, etc.).
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>1</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>40</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Massimo+Riva">Massimo Riva</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
									<dd>
						<span class="room"> </span>
						<span class="times">15:00 - 17:30 Fri - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017</span>
						</dd>
							
		
		
		
					<dt>Exam Group Code</dt>
			<dd>11</dd>
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>
                     </div>

                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Italian Studies Colloquium</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
  <div class="content brown-course-detail">
		
  	<h3>ITAL 2820 S01 <span class="crn">[<abbr title="Course Reference Number">CRN</abbr>: 16345]</span></h3>


  	The Italian Studies Colloquium is a forum for an exchange of ideas and work of the community of Italian scholars at Brown and invited outside scholars. Graduate students present their work in progress, and engage the work of faculty and visitors. They are expected to come prepared with informed questions on the topic presented. Presentations in both Italian and English. Instructor permission required.
		
		

		<dl>
		
		
		
		
		
		



					<dt>Term</dt>
			<dd>Fall 2017</dd>
		
					<dt>Credit Hours</dt>
			<dd>0.5</dd>
		
					<dt>Maximum Enrollment</dt>
			<dd>40</dd>
		
		


												
	<dt>Primary Instructor</dt>

		<dd>
		<div class="vcard">
			<div>
						<a class="url fn" href="http://directory.brown.edu/search?search_string=Ronald+L+Martinez">Ronald L Martinez</a>
			</div>
			
			
		</div>
	</dd>
				
			

	
					<dt>Meetings</dt>
									<dd>
						<span class="room"> </span>
						<span class="times">12:00 - 13:30 Fri - from Sep 6, 2017 to Dec 21, 2017</span>
						</dd>
							
		
		
		
					<dt>Exam Group Code</dt>
			<dd>12</dd>
		


		</dl>
  </div>

 </div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Courses for Fall 2017</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> <div class="content">



		<div class="course-section" id="ITAL">
			
				<ul class="course-list">
										<li id="ITAL0100">
					<h4>Elementary Italian</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Elective for students without previous training in Italian. No credit for first semester alone. Fundamentals of Italian grammar and development of skills in speaking, comprehension, and writing. Overview of contemporary Italian society. Four meetings per week, audio and video work, two Italian films.  Note:  This is a year course. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/italian-studies/COURSES/detail?term=201710&crn=15042">ITAL 0100 S01</a></h5>

						</div>

																							</dl>
						</div>

												</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="ITAL0300">
					<h4>Intermediate Italian I</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Review of the fundamentals of grammar, with emphasis on speaking and writing.  Reading of representative short stories.  Weekly compositions, presentations, and a paper.  Three Italian films.  Prerequisite:  ITAL 0100-0200, or ITAL 0110, or placement by examination.  Requirement for enrollment in the Bologna Program. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/italian-studies/COURSES/detail?term=201710&crn=15045">ITAL 0300 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Abbona-Sneider</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																				<div class="additional-sections">
															
																		
												<div class="section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/italian-studies/COURSES/detail?term=201710&crn=15049">ITAL 0300 S02</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Abbona-Sneider</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
														
																										</div>
												</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="ITAL0500">
					<h4>Advanced Italian I</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">The purpose of this advanced course is to improve speaking and writing skills by offering extensive practice in a variety of styles and forms. Students will discuss various aspects of contemporary Italian culture. Reading, analysis and class discussion of texts (articles, songs, pictures, short stories, movies and television), oral presentations, based on research, and a writing portfolio (compositions, essays, blog and a journal). Prerequisites: ITAL 0400, or placement by examination. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/italian-studies/COURSES/detail?term=201710&crn=15051">ITAL 0500 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Abbona-Sneider</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="ITAL1000G">
					<h4>Italian Identity</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">This course examines the process of the construction of Italian identity from National Unification until today. Through a close reading of Manzoni, De Amicis, Verga and Lampedusa’s works, we investigate the formation of Italian identity through language, literature, food, and opera. We will also examine the problems of Post-Unification Italy: the economic and cultural gap between North and South and the Southern Issue. Finally, we will examine documentaries and readings that assess Italy today to analyze the feeling of not-belonging and estrangement, and the problematic search for a cohesive identity in a multicultural Italy within the European Union. Taught in Italian. </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/italian-studies/COURSES/detail?term=201710&crn=16338">ITAL 1000G S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Fantarella</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="ITAL1010">
					<h4>Dante in English Translation: Dante's World and the Invention of Modernity</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Primarily for students with no knowledge of Italian. Given in English. Concentrators in Italian should enroll in ITAL 1610; they are expected to read the material in the original. Close study and discussion of Dante's deployment of systems of retribution in the Inferno and rehabilitation in the Purgatorio with a view to imagining a society based on love and resistant to the effects of nascent capitalism and the money economy. Dante's work summarizes and transforms the entire ancient and medieval tradition of literature, philosophy, and science. WRIT </div>
		
					<div class="sections">

																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>

					<div class="course-overview"> </div>

										<li id="ITAL1610">
					<h4>The Divina Commedia: Inferno and Purgatorio</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">A close reading of the first two canticles of Dante's poem in the light of contemporary European and American critical interpretations. In Italian. Enrollment limited to 40. </div>

										<li id="ITAL1920">
					<h4>Independent Study Project (Undergraduate)</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">Undergraduate Independent Study supervised by a member of the Italian Studies Faculty. Students may pursue independent research in order to prepare for their honors thesis or honors multimedia project, or they may enroll in the course in order to work individually with a faculty member on a specific area of Italian Studies not covered in the current course offerings.  Section numbers vary by instructor. Please check Banner for the correct section number and CRN to use when registering for this course. </div>

										<li id="ITAL2100">
					<h4>Introduction to Italian Studies</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">This seminar, a requirement for graduate students in Italian Studies, has three objectives: 1) to provide a panoramic view of the current research in the interdisciplinary field of Italian studies (literature, history, arts and media); 2) to provide a picture of the professional state of the field, within the framework of more global developments in academia and the job markets; 3) to provide useful information about the resources and the new tools and techniques for research available to students at Brown and elsewhere (special collections in the Brown libraries, digital resources such as data bases, electronic journals, web projects, etc.). </div>
		
					<div class="sections">
								
												
												<div class="section first-section">
												
							<h5><a href="/academics/italian-studies/COURSES/detail?term=201710&crn=16341">ITAL 2100 S01</a></h5>
														<dl>
																<dt>Primary Instructor</dt><dd>Riva</dd>
																							</dl>
						</div>
						
																					
																								</div>
						
				</li>
										<li id="ITAL2820">
					<h4>Italian Studies Colloquium</h4>
					<div class="course-overview">The Italian Studies Colloquium is a forum for an exchange of ideas and work of the community of Italian scholars at Brown and invited outside scholars. Graduate students present their work in progress, and engage the work of faculty and visitors. They are expected to come prepared with informed questions on the topic presented. Presentations in both Italian and English. Instructor permission required. </div>

<script type="text/javascript">
	// @todo: make show/hide link dynamically generated
	$(document).ready(function(){
	
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").hide();

		// add additional sections toggle link
		$(".course-list .additional-sections").each(function(i,el){
			var numSections = $(".section", $(this)).length;
			numSections = (numSections == 1) ? numSections + " additional section" : numSections + " additional sections";
			var anchor = $(this).parents("li").attr('id');
			$(this).after('<span class="section-count">[<a href="#' + anchor + '">Show ' + numSections + '</a>]</span>');
		});

		// now add the show/hide event listeners		
		$(".section-count").each(function(i,el){
			$("a", this).bind("click keypress", function(){
				$(".additional-sections", $(this).parents("li")).slideToggle("fast");
				window.location.hash = $(this).attr("href");
				if($(this).html().match(/Show/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
				} else if($(this).html().match(/Hide/)) {
					$(this).html($(this).html().replace("Hide", "Show"));
				}
				this.text(($('#toggle').text() == 'Show more') ? 'Show less' : 'Show more');
				return false;
			});
		});
		
		if (window.location.hash) {
			var hash = window.location.hash;
			if(hash.match(/#[0-9]{4}/)) {
				$(hash +  " .additional-sections").slideDown("fast");
				$(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html($(hash +  " a[href='"+hash+"']").html().replace("Show", "Hide"));
			}
		}

	});
</script>
 </div>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Graduate Program</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-13" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <h3 class="large">Application deadline for admissions Dec.15, 2017</h3>
<h3 class="large">Director of Graduate Studies:&nbsp;</h3>
<p>Professor Ronald Martinez - <a href="mailto:Ronald_Martinez@brown.edu">Ronald_Martinez@brown.edu</a></p>
<h3>Italian Studies PhD Program</h3>
<p>The Doctoral program in Italian Studies is aimed at preparing students for academic positions in a market that is shifting its traditional focus from language and literature teaching positions toward an interdisciplinary “cultural studies” perspective. One of the fundamental assets we offer our students, in preparation for their career, is advanced training and intensive experience in teaching language and culture at various levels, along with preparation in the most current research and teaching methodologies, including special training in the <a href="http://www.brown.edu/Departments/Italian_Studies/vhl_new/" target="_blank">digital humanities</a>.</p>
<h3 class="large">Interdisciplinary Graduate Program Description</h3>
<p><strong>Requirements for the Ph.D.</strong></p>
<p>There are three stages in the Ph.D. program:&nbsp;1) Preparation for Candidacy, which includes Coursework, the First Year Review and fulfillment of the Teaching and one of the two foreign languages required in the Language Requirement;&nbsp;2) Advancement to Candidacy, which includes the Preliminary Examination and the writing of an approved Dissertation Proposal; and&nbsp;3) the writing of a Dissertation in completion of the degree and the completion of the final foreign language requirement.   NOTA BENE: The Graduate School requires a total of 24 credits (24 enrollment units for residency requirement) to complete the Ph.D. degree. For students entering with an M.A. or Laurea,* up to 8 credits can be transferred from the M.A. or Laurea granting institution, upon Advancement to Candidacy. Credits reflect a combination of coursework, independent study and preparation for Examinations, etc., including the completion of the Dissertation (1 credit is assigned to each course, independent study, Preliminary Examination preparation, and Dissertation work).</p>
<p><strong>Preparation for Candidacy</strong></p>
<p>Course requirements.  At least 12 courses in Italian Studies are required of doctoral students. All courses must be taken at the 1000-, or 2000-level (Brown designates 1000-level courses as upper-level undergraduate courses and those at the 2000-level courses as graduate courses). The following are courses required of all graduate students:</p>
<p><strong>ITAL2100</strong> Introduction to Italian Studies (1st year or second year, depending on when course is offered, <span>or equivalent course, when course is not offered</span>). <br /><strong> ITAL2820</strong> Italian Studies Colloquium. In the first year, students may elect to take the Colloquium for credit, if they write short response papers on the presentations. Second-year students must take the Colloquium for credit, since they will be presenting their research in addition to participating in the colloquium. When in residency, all students are expected to attend the colloquium and all students should sign up for the course as auditors. &nbsp;<strong>ITAL2900</strong> Teaching Methodology (no later than the second year). Students are encouraged to take Teaching Methodology during the first year whenever possible. Beginning in the academic year 2009-2010, students are required to pass the course with the grade of “B” if they are to be allowed to teach during a subsequent semester. Students with less than a “B” in the course will go on automatic warning, and be required to repeat the coursework.  <br />Graduate students are required to take three courses in Medieval/Early Modern Italian Studies (one must be on Dante), and three courses in Modern/Contemporary Italian Studies. Graduate students are also required to take at least one course in three out of four disciplinary fields (Italian literature; Italian history and anthropology; history of Italian art and architecture; Italian film and media studies). However, one course can fulfill both the chronological and the field requirement (for example: a course in Renaissance art can fulfill both the Medieval/Early Modern and the field requirement). In either area (Medieval/Early Modern or Modern/Contemporary Italian Studies) students may enroll in one independent study course (ITAL 2920: Reading and Research) in order to fulfill their requirements in that area.</p>
<p>Students entering the program with a fellowship normally take 8 courses or independent studies in their first year. Students entering with a Teaching Assistantship are permitted to take up to 6 courses or independent studies.</p>
<p><em>Transfer credits:&nbsp;</em><span>Students transferring into the graduate program from other graduate institutions or from Italian universities are expected to complete the first year of residence at Brown before transfer credits can be recognized. It is possible to transfer a maximum of eight credits toward the Ph.D. degree. Students may get specific information about how to transfer credits from either Mona Delgado or the Director of Graduate Studies.</span></p>
<p><em>Incompletes:&nbsp;</em><span>The faculty views any incomplete grades that are not accounted for by circumstances over which the student has no control as danger signals. Students who take incompletes in course work find themselves in a particularly difficult situation. Not only does the incomplete suggest that they are having trouble working with graduate school conditions, but it limits the amount of evidence that would be available for evaluation. Furthermore, the work of the subsequent semester suffers badly if the student is finishing up one semester while beginning another. Accordingly, students should make every effort in order to avoid incompletes; if one proves unavoidable, the student should discuss the reasons for the incomplete with the instructor and the Graduate Advisor, so that it can be explained. Under normal circumstances, students will not be permitted to have more than one INC per semester. According to the Handbook of the Graduate School (Part VII, G) “an instructor may allow a student to complete course work after the normal deadline, but after one year, the permission of a Dean is required for a grade to be given.” Finally, graduate students in Italian Studies should be aware that outstanding grades of INC might jeopardize their TA-ships, according to the handbook regulations of the Graduate School (Part VII, G).</span></p>
<p><em>Grades:&nbsp;</em><span>In general, “A” or “A-“ grades should signal superior, not merely good, graduate performance in course work and on papers. “B” grades should indicate good, solid graduate-level performance. Grades in the “C” range indicate work considerably below that standard. “C” grades do afford graduate credit, but will not be counted by the Italian Studies Dept. towards the satisfaction of the departmental course requirement. Such coursework will have to be repeated again for credit. The receipt of a “C” grade in one or more of the required courses will automatically lead to a warning status.</span></p>
<p><em> First Year Review</em></p>
<p>At the end of the first year, each student – whether entering with a B.A. or an M.A. – will participate in a review of his or her progress in the program. This review by the Department Graduate Committee (GC) will be based on a sample of work completed during the year (e.g. seminar papers) and on reports by the student’s instructors. The Graduate Committee will meet with the student to discuss the materials submitted and the student’s performance and to advise the student about possible fields for the Preliminary Examination.</p>
<p>On the basis of the First Year Review, the GC will make a recommendation to the department as to whether the student may continue in the Ph.D. program. The committee can recommend that the student proceed towards advanced candidacy; or the GC may determine that the student should not continue in the Ph.D. program. In the latter case, the student may be recommended to the Graduate School for a terminal Masters degree, provided that s/he has satisfactorily completed eight (8) courses.</p>
<p>Students who have entered the department with an M.A. and who have completed all the first year requirements may elect to receive a Brown University M.A. at their discretion.</p>
<p><em> Foreign Language Requirement</em></p>
<p>2 Foreign languages, other than English and Italian, are required. Examinations in other languages are administered by the relevant departments, and coursework in the FL at 1000-level or above may also fulfill the requirement.</p>
<p><em> Teaching Requirement </em></p>
<p>A minimum of two years of teaching experience is required for the degree.</p>
<p><strong>Advancement to Candidacy</strong></p>
<p><em>Preliminary Examination</em></p>
<p>Graduate students are expected to take the Preliminary Examination (PE) by the end of the 5th-semester (Semester 1 of the third year). Successful completion of the PE authorizes the candidate to proceed with the dissertation proposal. All course requirements and the First Year Review must be successfully completed prior to the PE. At least one language requirement must be fulfilled to advance to candidacy.</p>
<p>There are three necessary steps for the preparation and completion of the PE: 1) The student must define his or her fields of examination and form a PE committee; 2) He or she must select a list of texts and other materials for the examination in consultation with the PE committee; 3) The student must take the examination.</p>
<p><em>Defining the fields and constituting a committee:&nbsp;</em><span>By the end of the second year for students entering the program with a B.A. or the end of the third semester for those entering with an M.A., candidates must define three fields, one primary and two secondary. The candidate must also form a committee of at least two faculty members in Italian Studies and designate a chair for that committee. It is the student’s responsibility to approach a prospective chair and ask whether he or she is willing to serve on the committee. It is also the student’s responsibility to make arrangements with the committee members in order to prepare for the PE.</span></p>
<p>Taken together, the three fields should delimit academic area(s) in which the student is preparing to teach, as well the scholarly context(s) for the student's projected research. The configuration of the fields for all students will be as follows:</p>
<p>*Field 1: Medieval/Early Modern or Modern/Contemporary Italian Studies. *Field 2: A theoretical, disciplinary or interdisciplinary perspective within field 1 (or across fields): ex. microhistory, history of the book, gender studies, literary theory, political symbolism, film studies, computing for the humanities, etc.; <br />*Field 3: An elective field such as a specific topic, theme or author within field 1: ex. Dante or Boccaccio studies, Renaissance or Baroque theatre and architecture, history of the family, fascism, (post)colonialism, migrant literature and film, etc.</p>
<p><em>Reading Lists for the PE</em></p>
<p>The candidate must submit three field lists, one for each field, of at least 40-30-20 (for each list respectively) key scholarly books or the equivalent materials, such as articles and chapters, or media materials (films, etc.). All of these texts should be chosen in consultation with the student’s committee members, and the final lists must be approved by the PE committee.</p>
<p><strong>The Preliminary Examination</strong></p>
<p><em>General Overview</em></p>
<p><em>&nbsp;</em>The PE consists in a written and an oral part. Part One (written examination): A take-home written exam, consisting in answers to three questions, one for each field, formulated by the PE committee and based on the lists previously submitted and approved. The candidate will have one week (Friday 9 a.m. to the following Friday 5 p.m.) to complete the assignment. Part Two (oral examination): A two-hour discussion of the written exam and field lists. This part of the exam will begin from but not be limited to the student’s written exam and the core field bibliographies. It will probe the student’s understanding of his or her field and the debates within them. The purpose of the PE is to establish both the breadth and the depth of the student’s competence and knowledge in those areas where he or she plans to teach and do research. Upon the completion of the PE, the committee will come to one of the following determinations: a) Pass; or b) directed to retake the exam. Students may retake the exam once.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Specific Procedures and Guidelines for Preliminary Examinations in Italian Studies</strong></p>
<p><strong>For the written portion of the exam:</strong></p>
<p><strong></strong>1. Students will receive via e-mail a list of questions divided according to the three bibliographies that have organized the student’s preparation for the exam.</p>
<p>2. From these questions (two questions per bibliographic list) the student will choose one question per bibliographic list to which to respond.</p>
<p>3. Students may respond to the questions either in Italian or in English.</p>
<p>4. Responses should be typewritten.</p>
<p>5. For each question, students should write approximately 2000 words, including footnotes.</p>
<p>6. Students should include a bibliography of texts consulted. The bibliography does not count toward the word limit.</p>
<p>7. Students are expected to work alone on their responses to the questions, but the written portion of the exam is considered a “take home” and therefore students may consult books and notes in order to write their response.</p>
<p>8. Standards of academic citation and academic honesty apply to the exam. Students should cite texts upon which they have based their arguments or from which they have cited directly. Considering the short length allotted for the responses, lengthy direct quotes should be avoided.</p>
<p><strong>Time Frame and Best Procedures for Scheduling the Written and Oral Portion of the Exam:</strong></p>
<p><strong></strong>1. Whenever possible, the students’ written exam should begin on a Friday with the receipt of the questions and end on the subsequent Friday with the submission of the responses via e-mail to the chair of the committee.</p>
<p>2. The oral portion of the preliminary exam will take place on the Tuesday following the Friday that the student has submitted her/his responses.</p>
<p><strong>Oral Portion of the Exam:</strong></p>
<p><strong></strong>1. The oral portion of the exam is approximately one and a half hours of discussion of the written exam and the student’s reading in the three bibliographies.</p>
<p>2. The oral portion of the exam will be organized to examine the student’s understanding of his or her field and the debates within them.</p>
<p>3. The exam will be structured with the following guidelines in mind: Each bibliography will receive about one-half hour of discussion.</p>
<p><em>The Dissertation Proposal</em></p>
<p>After passing the preliminary examination, and no later than September of the fourth year, the candidate must defend her or his dissertation proposal. He or she forms a dissertation committee, writes a dissertation proposal, en route to writing the dissertation and finishing the degree.</p>
<p>It is the student's responsibility to approach a faculty member and ask if he or she is willing to serve as dissertation director. The candidate then constitutes a dissertation committee, in consultation with the dissertation director. The dissertation committee normally consists of three faculty members, at least two of whom must be in Italian Studies or affiliated with the Department. (In some cases, a candidate may request an additional faculty member – including one from another university – when it is necessary to cover unusual interests or fields pertinent to the dissertation.) The dissertation committee is often the same as the Preliminary Examination committee, but this is not required.   The candidate then writes a dissertation proposal in consultation with committee members.</p>
<p>The dissertation proposal should furnish a clear description of the object or concern of the study, the methodological, historical or literary issues raised in the dissertation, the scholarly context and bibliography within which the work positions itself, as well as its the organization and structure.   The dissertation is generally a book-length study. It must constitute an original contribution to its fields of concern and meet the highest standards of scholarly competence. Even with a firm idea about the dissertation topic, the student should not assume that he or she can write the proposal quickly and gain fast approval by the committee. Since this is probably the first time a student will conduct research of this scale, the committee will want to ensure that the proposal demonstrates not only intellectual and scholarly depth, range, and significance; the committee will also be concerned that the project is feasible and can be completed within a reasonable amount of time.</p>
<p>When the candidate and the dissertation director believe the proposal is ready, the committee will hold a dissertation proposal meeting with the candidate. At the thesis proposal meeting, the candidate will summarize her/his essay as if it were a scholarly paper presented in a lecture or at a conference. A discussion will follow, with the members of the Dissertation Committee first taking turns in asking questions. Questions may probe the topic of the proposal; its methodology; theoretical premises; accuracy; and thoroughness of preliminary research. Questions should lead to the clearer formulation of the dissertation project.</p>
<p>The committee will either approve the proposal or recommend revisions. The student must submit a file copy of the final, approved proposal, along with a cover sheet signed by all members of the committee, to the Director of Graduate Studies. A file of previous dissertation proposals is kept in the Italian Studies Department office and is available for students to consult.</p>
<p><strong>Dissertation</strong></p>
<p><strong></strong>The dissertation is a substantial work of scholarship or criticism, generally ranging between 200 and 300 double-spaced pages. There are many considerations I choosing a topic. Given the structure of the job market, the dissertation topic plays an important role in identifying a job applicant in the minds of prospective employers. The student should seek advice on this aspect of the dissertation topic, as well as on other issues. The topic should be clearly defined and its completion feasible within a reasonable period of time. [Nota bene: Brown University regulations require that students complete their dissertation within five years of being admitted to candidacy. Exceptions to this rule are made only with the consent of the Department and the Graduate Council.]</p>
<p>Revised June 2012</p>
<p>* Laurea quadriennale, or “specialistica (3+2 year).</p>
<p><a href="http://www.brown.edu/academics/gradschool/application-information">Graduate School On-line Application&nbsp;</a></p>

        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">Alumni News</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-222" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <h3></h3>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong>Anna Aresi, PhD 2016</strong><span><span class="il"><br /></span></span><span>Anna&nbsp;Aresi graduated summa cum laude from the University of Padua, Italy, in Classics and Italian Literature and Philology. She received her Ph.D. degree with a dissertation entitled&nbsp;<em>Modernism through Dante: T. S. Eliot, Clemente Rebora, and Osip Mandelstam in May 2016.&nbsp;</em>Her dissertation explores the reception of Dante in European modernism, focusing on how the reception of Dante influenced modernist poetics.&nbsp;Anna’s areas of interest include: Dante Studies, Italian Modern and Contemporary Literature, Italian and European Modernism, Reception and Translation Studies, Second Language Acquisition, and Contemplative Pedagogy. She is the director of the "Poetry in Translation" section of the journal&nbsp;<em>Mosaici&nbsp;</em>(<a href="http://mosaici.org.uk/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">mosaici.org.uk</a>). To view Anna's research profile, please visit:&nbsp;</span><span><a href="https://brown.academia.edu/AnnaAresi" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">https://brown.academia.edu/AnnaAresi</a>. To view Anna's Online Teaching Portfolio, please visit:&nbsp;<a href="http://aaresi.weebly.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">aaresi.weebly.com</a>&nbsp;(password upon request).</span><span>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a href="mailto:Anna_Aresi@brown.edu" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">Anna_Aresi@brown.edu</a></span></p>
<h4><span>&nbsp;</span></h4>
<h4><span>&nbsp;</span></h4>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong>Francesco Borghesi, PhD 2004.&nbsp;<br /></strong><a href="http://sydney.edu.au/arts/slc/staff/profiles/francesco.borghesi.php" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">Francesco Borghesi</a><span>&nbsp;is currently Senior Lecturer of Italian at the University of Sydney, NSW, Australia. Among his recent publications, he co-edited (with Michael Papio, Ph.D. 1998, and Massimo Riva) the Cambridge U.P. edition of G. Pico della Mirandola,&nbsp;</span><em>On Human Dignity,</em><span>&nbsp;published in 2012.</span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong>Elena Daniele, PhD 2014</strong><br />Originally from Padova, Elena Daniele studied cultural anthropology and ethnology at La Sapienza University in Rome and graduated in 2005 after completing field work in the Amazon forest. She then received a M.A. in Italian teaching methodology from Università per Stranieri di Perugia in 2006. At Brown, she completed her dissertation, entitled "Representations of American Cannibalism in Early Modern Travel Literature" and received her Ph.D. at the 2014 commencement. Her research interest lie at the intersection of literature, anthropology, history, and the practices of ethnographic writing; her teaching experience includes Italian instruction at Brown University, Università per Stranieri di Perugia, and Ateneo Salesiano in Rome. She was the recepient of the John Carter Brown Library Stuart Fellowship for the academic year 2012-2013. She was the co-curator, with K. Dian Kriz (History of Art and Architecture), &nbsp;of the JCB Library’s Fall 2013 Exhibition in conjuction with the conference entitled "Sugar and Beyond” (October 25-26, 2013), and focused on sugar in the early modern period, especially its bibliographical and visual legacies. She is currently teaching at Tulane University. <a href="mailto:Elena_Daniele@alumni.brown.edu">Elena_Daniele@alumni.brown.edu</a></p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong>Lianca Carlesi</strong><br /><span class="thumbnail-wrapper inline inline-left" style="width:133px;"><img src="https://www.brown.edu/academics/italian-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.italian-studies/files/images/L.Carlesi.jpg" alt="Lianca Carlesi" title="Lianca Carlesi"  class="image image-_original " width="125" height="167" /><span class="caption"><strong>Lianca Carlesi</strong></span></span>Lianca Carlesi Ph.D. 2017, graduated summa cum laude from the University of Bologna where&nbsp;she earned a Master Degree in Contemporary Italian Literature with a thesis on a comparative reading of a selection of&nbsp;Italian Resistance novels. She started her Ph.D. at Brown in 2010, and she is currently in her fellowship year. At Brown she&nbsp;taught beginning and intermediate level Italian courses, she was a TA for an Italian culture course, and she organized the&nbsp;2014 edition of Chiasmi, the Brown-Harvard Graduate Student Conference. Her main interest is Twentieth Century Italian&nbsp;literature, with particular regard to postwar and Resistance literature. Her dissertation project focused on Cesare Pavese,&nbsp;especially on the last years of his literary and intellectual activity.&nbsp;<a href="mailto:Lianca_Carlesi@brown.edu" rel="nofollow">Lianca_Carlesi@brown.edu</a></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong>Wuming Chang</strong></p>
<p><span class="thumbnail-wrapper inline inline-left" style="width:108px;"><img src="https://www.brown.edu/academics/italian-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.italian-studies/files/images/W.Chang_.thumbnail.JPG" alt="Wuming Chang" title="Wuming Chang"  class="image image-thumbnail " width="100" height="100" /><span class="caption"><strong>Wuming Chang</strong></span></span>Wuming Chang, PhD 2017, wrote his dissertation on Rhetoric as Imitation of the City and the Cosmos in Dante's Comedy, where he examined the intertexual relationship between rhetorical texts (manuals, political epistles, orations) and Dante's poem, especially in its cosmological passages.&nbsp; His interests center on the relationship between Dante and aspects of Medieval Latin culture, such as political rhetoric, philosophy, and the reception of classics.&nbsp; Wuming was born in Beijing, where he received a B.A. in philosophy at Peking University and also acted extensively.&nbsp; In his free time he enjoys all kinds of music, theatre and poetry, and stutteringly debates social and philosophical issues with friends.&nbsp;<a href="mailto:wuming_chang@brown.edu" rel="nofollow">wuming_chang@brown.edu</a></p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong><a href="http://www.hofstra.edu/faculty/fac_profiles.cfm?id=222" rel="nofollow">Simone Castaldi</a>, PhD 2002</strong>, Associate Professor, Hofstra University</p>
<p><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5k-Sv9A6fYE" rel="nofollow">Dr. Simone castaldi yo translate new series of "Corto Maltese" </a>comics for the english reader.</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong>Amanda Minervini, PhD 2012.&nbsp;<br /></strong><a href="http://salemstate.academia.edu/AmandaMinervini" rel="nofollow">Amanda Minervini</a><span>&nbsp;currently teaches Italian and German language and culture at Salem State University. Her research interests are focused on the interaction of politics and religion, in particular on the representations of St. Francis of Assisi during Italian Fascism. With the aim to foster the dialogue between academic worlds, she has been translating political theory texts by Wendy Brown, Giorgio Agamben and Carlo Galli for Italian and Anglo-American audiences. She recently started working on contemporary political documentaries about Italy and her essay "</span><em>Uccidete la democrazia e Girlfriend in a Coma: il nuovo documentario politico sull'Italia</em><span>" is forthcoming in Hope, William, Luciana D'Arcangeli, and Silvana Serra.&nbsp;</span><em>Un nuovo cinema politico italiano?</em><span>&nbsp;Vol 2</span></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p><strong>Mauro Resmini, PhD 2014.<br /></strong>Mauro Resmini received his BA in Media Studies from the Department of Political Science at Università Cattolica del Sacro Cuore in Milan (Italy) in 2003; then he received his MA (laurea magistralis summa cum laude) in Theory and Techniques of Media Communication – with a specific focus on film theory – from the Department of Literature and Philosophy at the same university in 2006, with a dissertation about the role of the face in contemporary post-noir cinema. After graduation, he worked as a journalist and film critic, and he pursued his collaboration with the academia as a teaching assistant at the Università Cattolica del Sacro Cuore for the “Film Semiology” and “History and Critique of Cinema” classes. He is also one of the contributors of “Segnocinema”, a review of cinema and film studies, for which he wrote various essays since 2005. At Brown, he is completed a special PhD program in Visual Studies, sponsored by the Department of Italian Studies and the Department of Modern Culture and Media. His research interests include film theory, semiotics, psychoanalysis, contemporary American and Italian cinema, digital cinema and comics. He is currently living and teaching in Washington, D.C. <a href="mailto:Mauro_Resmini@alumni.brown.edu">Mauro_Resmini@alumni.brown.edu</a></p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td><span class="thumbnail-wrapper inline inline-left" style="width:134px;"><img src="https://www.brown.edu/academics/italian-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.italian-studies/files/images/81ElTdaT9lL._SL1500_.preview.jpg" alt="Film Sound in Italy" title="Film Sound in Italy"  class="image image-preview " width="126" height="195" /><span class="caption"><strong>Film Sound in Italy</strong></span></span><br /></td>
<td>
<h3 class="large"><strong>Antonella Sisto, Ph.D., 2011</strong></h3>
<h3 class="large highlight"><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Film-Sound-Italy-Listening-Screen/dp/113738770X" target="_blank" rel="nofollow">Film Sound in Italy. Listening to the Screen, Palgrave-McMillan, 2014</a></h3>
<p>Considering films as audio-visual creations opens new inroads into the cultural practice, politics, and aesthetics of the soundtrack. This book is critical and trans-disciplinary engagement with cinema in Italy that examines the national archive of film based on sound ...</p>
<div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<table>

<tr>
<td><span class="thumbnail-wrapper inline inline-left" style="width:183px;"><img src="https://www.brown.edu/academics/italian-studies/sites/brown.edu.academics.italian-studies/files/images/Vika and Nico_1.jpg" alt="Vika and Nico" title="Vika and Nico"  class="image image-brown_slides_main_column " width="175" height="263" /><span class="caption"><strong>Vika and Nico</strong></span></span></td>
<td>
<h3><span class="large"><strong>Vika Zafrin PhD 2007</strong>.</span> After completing her Ph. in Humanities Computing, Vika took a step sideways and is now Institutional Repository Librarian at Boston University. <span>She helps researchers understand the implications of open access in the academic setting, and manages BU's institutional repository&nbsp;</span><a href="http://open.bu.edu/xmlui/" rel="nofollow">OpenBU</a><span>. She also serves as the Executive Secretary of the&nbsp;</span><a href="http://ach.org/" rel="nofollow">Association for Computers and the Humanities</a><span>. When not at work or conferences, she cooks up a storm, spends time with friends and family, and horses around with her toddler Nico.</span></h3>
</td>
</tr>

  <div id="content">
    <div class="marginator">
                  <div class="columns no-right-column">
        <h1 class="article-title  with-tabs">FAQs for Prospective Graduate Students</h1>                        <div id="body-content" class="second-column column main-column">
                                                  <div class="clear-block"> 
<article id="node-195" class="main-article node">








  <div class="content">
        <p>Q: Do I have to take the GREs?<br />A: The Graduate Record Examination (GRE) is required. Tests should be taken well in advance of the application deadline of December 15.</p>
<p>Q: Does the department require that students achieve a minimum score on the GRE general and/or subject test?<br />A: The department has no minimum GRE score requirement, nor do we have an official policy stipulating an acceptable range of GRE scores.</p>
<p>Q: Do I have to take the TOEFL exam if my native language is not English?<br />A: Yes. Brown University requires this exam.</p>
<p>Q: Is a writing sample required?<br />A: Yes. We would like writing samples in both Italian and English.</p>
<p>Q: Is an interview required?<br />A: No, but it is strongly recommended that you have an on-site or telephone interview with the faculty who work in your area(s) of interest.</p>
<p>Q: Do you have a terminal MA degree?<br />A: No. Students receive an MA as part of their progress to the PhD.</p>
<p>Q: Does the Department encourage students to take courses outside the Department?<br />A: Yes—students often take seminars, and occasionally lecture courses in other departments and also at other institutions such as Harvard.</p>
<p>For further questions please e-mail: <a href="mailto:Italian_Studies@brown.edu">Italian_Studies@brown.edu</a></p>
  </div>

	



  <div class="clear-block">
    <div class="meta">

			
	    
		</div><!-- end .meta -->
	</div>

</article>
 </div>
                     </div>
